through the ConfigDef class and its nested ConfigKey class for configuration documentation. Rather than using Java annotations with @interface, Kafka uses a fluent declarative API pattern for configuration definition.\\n\\n**Core Implementation Files:**\\n\\n1. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/ConfigDef.java` - Contains the ConfigDef class which serves as the main configuration specification mechanism. It includes the nested static ConfigKey class which holds metadata about individual configuration parameters including name, type, default value, validator, importance level, and documentation string. The ConfigDef class provides:\\n   - `define()` method: fluent API for defining configuration keys\\n   - `validate()` method: validates complete configurations\\n   - `parse()` method: parses raw configuration values\\n   - `toHtml()` method: generates HTML documentation from the configuration definitions\\n\\n2. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/AbstractConfig.java` - The abstract base class for all configuration classes. It holds ConfigDef instances and provides infrastructure for configuration parsing, validation, and value retrieval.\\n\\n**Configuration Documentation Generators:**\\n\\n1. OVERVIEW_DOC static members.\\n\\n2. `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/tools/PredicateDoc.java` - Generates HTML documentation for Kafka Connect predicates.\\n\\n**AbstractConfig
